  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_80bd6f6e-4e07-43c1-b75a-9a70ff60c6ef'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer12716766518844001777">My heart is shattered, and my anxiety has spiked! What an ending! <br/><br/>I love the rush that one gets when reading an intricate story like this, but oh my, could the author not have chosen to be perhaps a little more gentle with my emotions! <br/><br/>I am both angry and shattered!! <br/><br/>I'm angry at the injustice I have just 'witnessed,' and I am shattered by what happened to these pour characters! And to just end with, "he's here," both frustrated me, terrified me, and satisfied me, because who doesn't enjoy a goo</span>
  <span id="freeText12716766518844001777" style="display:none">My heart is shattered, and my anxiety has spiked! What an ending! <br /><br />I love the rush that one gets when reading an intricate story like this, but oh my, could the author not have chosen to be perhaps a little more gentle with my emotions! <br /><br />I am both angry and shattered!! <br /><br />I'm angry at the injustice I have just 'witnessed,' and I am shattered by what happened to these pour characters! And to just end with, "he's here," both frustrated me, terrified me, and satisfied me, because who doesn't enjoy a good cliff hanger? Arrrgg. <br /><br />But here we go; I have not written a review in forever, so I might be a bit rusty. <br /><br />I enjoyed this book for a few reasons; 1. I loved the books before this one, so of course, I would enjoy returning to the world the author has created. 2. the author himself always brings a new and original way of writing, so I never know what to expect. And 3. I know I am in for a wild ride. <br /><br />This book is truly sad and terrifying but amazing because we see more than we did in the previous books. These characters were great and tragic (for the most part), and I was kept intrigued throughout. <br /><br />I guessed who the real Raven Heiress was but how the reveal came about was out of nowhere. And yet, that would not be the real shock factor of this book!!!! But just another element of the story to add further surprise. I loved that! And I loved the mystery surrounding the 'Higher of Evlon.' He was pure evil, but my heart breaks for him, given how I know his backstory! I love that about this author; he truly knows how to offer dimension to his characters and give them double layers of personality and motive. <br /><br />I cannot wait for more, and I really hope to see this series and this author take off someday.</span>

<div id="review_3544522536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3544522536" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82730476-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528196723p2/82730476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3544522536?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/82730476-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3544522536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10618534797394577970">I forgot how much of a fan I am of this author, seeing as it has been a long time between releases. Though I was not disappointed, I will say that my favorite in the series is still The Missing. But with that said, the ending of this book shook me so much more. <br/><br/>The prologue was one of the best individual chapters I've ever read. There was so much pain in it that I thought, 'what a way to start a book.' Then the story kicks off with typical Forysth mystery, luring me deeper and deeper into the pa</span>
  <span id="freeText10618534797394577970" style="display:none">I forgot how much of a fan I am of this author, seeing as it has been a long time between releases. Though I was not disappointed, I will say that my favorite in the series is still The Missing. But with that said, the ending of this book shook me so much more. <br /><br />The prologue was one of the best individual chapters I've ever read. There was so much pain in it that I thought, 'what a way to start a book.' Then the story kicks off with typical Forysth mystery, luring me deeper and deeper into the pages, all the while a dark atmosphere gradually starts setting in. From the beginning, I could definitely sense a sinister presence lurking close to the main characters. <br /><br />Like the books before this, the world-building was off the charts and done skilfully and subtly and without taking away or diverting from the actual story. I enjoyed the dynamic between the Singing Elves and Saph Elves and how they were both amazed by the Moon Elves, and how, through their interactions, I was able to learn more and more about the world Forsyth has created. <br /><br />Again, the way it was written was typical Forsyth style, who always delivers a new and unexpected way of story-telling. I think it was clever telling one story three times but by three different people. However, I did feel that certain sections could have been looked over, seeing as we visit those parts a couple of times before it becomes stale. But this was a minor draw-back. <br /><br />The ending (as I have said) shook me! There were a few shock factors throughout the story, but the ending was the true monster. Hopefully, I don't have to wait long for the next installment, but seeing as The Raven Heiress was worth the wait, I do not doubt that the next release will be worth the wait too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10618534797394577970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3544804686" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3544804686" />
    <a title="Edward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87400615-edward"><img alt="Edward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538210725p2/87400615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3544804686?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/87400615-edward">Edward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3544804686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16054971325432589706">Intense! <br/><br/>These books seem to me as if they just keep getting more and more intense. This one takes the cake! <br/><br/>Where do I begin? <br/><br/>The beginning is morbid and full of mystery, which I appreciate. From the get-go, something had already happened, and it was the reader's journey to discover what! I enjoyed that because, from chapter one, I was already hooked! <br/><br/>I have always appreciated the writing of this author, but I felt as if the writing in this book is way better than in the previous ones. <br/><br/>There we</span>
  <span id="freeText16054971325432589706" style="display:none">Intense! <br /><br />These books seem to me as if they just keep getting more and more intense. This one takes the cake! <br /><br />Where do I begin? <br /><br />The beginning is morbid and full of mystery, which I appreciate. From the get-go, something had already happened, and it was the reader's journey to discover what! I enjoyed that because, from chapter one, I was already hooked! <br /><br />I have always appreciated the writing of this author, but I felt as if the writing in this book is way better than in the previous ones. <br /><br />There were large amounts of description, and I felt like I was walking the halls of the Evlon House. I felt like I could see the portrait of the moon elf king. Although I will admit that I didn't get scared reading this, and though I am sure the author intended the book to be scary, I was more intrigued.<br /><br />I enjoyed the characters, and I was obviously rooting for Orlan Efshas to 'win the girl'! And yet, knowing how this author enjoys dropping wild plot twists, it would have been wiser of me to remain instead neutral throughout! My mistake! <br /><br />Which brings me to the book's conclusion! I'd say the words intense and brutal are the best words to describe it. I was looking for where the twist would come from, and I thought I'd spotted it. But what I found was the 'the real Heiress' was not the book's primary shocker, but perhaps a diversion for the real build-up. <br /><br />Well done to the author, now let's not wait a whole year for the next one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16054971325432589706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1700647218037103966">I started this last night and finished it this morning! <br/><br/>The best thing about Goodreads is the opportunity to immediately jump onto a review screen and express how a book made you feel! If not for Goodreads, I'd simply explode after reading a book like this! <br/><br/>It's fantasy, my favorite genre, but filled with shocking twists that I want to scream! The world is so fascinating and exciting but also dark and tragic. I am convinced that this is the most tragic in the series and that is saying a lot! <br/><br/>I w</span>
  <span id="freeText1700647218037103966" style="display:none">I started this last night and finished it this morning! <br /><br />The best thing about Goodreads is the opportunity to immediately jump onto a review screen and express how a book made you feel! If not for Goodreads, I'd simply explode after reading a book like this! <br /><br />It's fantasy, my favorite genre, but filled with shocking twists that I want to scream! The world is so fascinating and exciting but also dark and tragic. I am convinced that this is the most tragic in the series and that is saying a lot! <br /><br />I was immediately captivated by the prologue and pulled into the story from chapter 1. I could not put my tablet down until about chapter 6 when I started feeling sleepy. This morning I jumped back into the book and after a minor break, I finished it with ease! <br /><br />The Saphian's side of the story was a great read, but when it was Naslas's turn, I sensed I shouldn't be so trusting so soon in the story, and began wondering if the Saphian was lying all this time. But then it was Arrandla's turn, and her chapters quickly became my favorite. Hers was emotive, relatable and the most interesting, and it was in her chapters that I learned the truth. <br /><br />The Higher of Evlon was scary, but I didn't hate him until the epilogue. I was so shocked by what he did. <br /><br />Other reviews were right. The shock factor at the end of this book was a real monster and though I enjoy this author, I hope one day we get a book that is not so gruesome and perhaps has a happy ending. <br /><br />I feel oppressed, which is not a good feeling, but besides this drawback, I really enjoyed this installment and I must recommend it to all my GR friends! You never know what you're going to get with these books. <br /><br />Thanks for reading! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2799574641812958383">My heart broke for Durasian during The Missing, and now my heart breaks for him in The Raven Heiress! My heart feels heavy while writing this, and I am not sure if that's a positive thing or not. <br/><br/>Without giving anything away, I was so sad to see what the former Higher of the Olian Glades becomes and because I can so imagine that happening to someone (not exactly becoming a ghost, but becoming almost mad!)   <span id="freeText2799574641812958383" style="display:none">My heart broke for Durasian during The Missing, and now my heart breaks for him in The Raven Heiress! My heart feels heavy while writing this, and I am not sure if that's a positive thing or not. <br /><br />Without giving anything away, I was so sad to see what the former Higher of the Olian Glades becomes and because I can so imagine that happening to someone (not exactly becoming a ghost, but becoming almost mad!) It is truly heartbreaking, and leave it to this author to take the reader to the deepest, rawest parts of his characters. I suppose making us feel and empathize with them is what he does! <br /><br />But here are my thoughts! <br /><br />Obviously, I loved this book! I loved Arrandle/Fenixia, and at some point, I was undecided about the Saphian, but eventually grew to like him. Both he and the Avadad-elf had sly motives, but in the end, the Saphian was sweet and determined, and his vulnerability in the temple leader chapters was heartbreaking! I just wanted to reach into the pages and hug him! But also, to save him from the end of this story, from this author!!! I want to cry now!! <br /><br />I loved the way the author told this story, seeing the story through the eyes of three different perspectives. I knew who the Raven Heiress was the entire time and was not exactly surprised when she was revealed! But just when I thought I had figured the author's mysteries out, bam! I get an ending that came out of know where and which made me gasp out loud (that's never happened to me before with the books I read!)<br /><br />What can I say? It's all sad! SAD, SAD, SAD! <br /><br />I'd like to say thank you to Jeremy Forsyth for the free copy! I love your imagination and your ability to bring that imagination to life! I recommend this author to everyone who loves original fantasy! </span>

  <span id="freeText12883773488943148181" style="display:none">Brilliant!! The way this author manages to execute his endings is just epic! <br /><br />I knew something was coming. <div id="review_3544772670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3544772670" />
    <a title="SonOfYork" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82688455-sonofyork"><img alt="SonOfYork" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528098887p2/82688455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3544772670?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SonOfYork" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SonOfYork" href="/user/show/82688455-sonofyork">SonOfYork</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3544772670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9884412823336247621">While most authors focus their stories around big political and dynastic characters like kings, queens, and ministers, I've noticed that this author prefers his readers to witness the high up top power struggles from the ground. <br/><br/>The main characters in this book are three children whose parents are, in fact, high stake players, but they themselves aren't. They are regular people, and through them, we learn about what is going on at court, and in palaces, while their own personal challenges happen</span>
  <span id="freeText9884412823336247621" style="display:none">While most authors focus their stories around big political and dynastic characters like kings, queens, and ministers, I've noticed that this author prefers his readers to witness the high up top power struggles from the ground. <br /><br />The main characters in this book are three children whose parents are, in fact, high stake players, but they themselves aren't. They are regular people, and through them, we learn about what is going on at court, and in palaces, while their own personal challenges happen around them. <br /><br />I have always wondered what fascinating stories take place among the peasants while great wars happen among the nobles, and in this series, I get to see some of these stories. <br /><br />Again, I was impressed with this author and must congratulate him for once more crafting a story with imaginative flair and constructs. <br /><br />Despair and loss is a constant underlining theme here, and given what we know about what happens in the previous book, this theme makes sense. Other themes include prejudice, racism, and hierarchy. There was no love, romance, or battle, but mystery and deception. <br /><br />Throughout the story, the author lures you further and further into the pages, where the discovery at the end is shocking, but all so thrilling if you're into great surprises. I thoroughly enjoy the shock factors one finds in books and movies and it's precisely why I gravitate towards authors like this because I never know what to expect. <br /><br />Each book has been written in a different way, and in each book, there is a massive surprise waiting at the end. I sensed something was coming the entire time which added to the excitement. <br /><br />Jeremy Forsyth, well done, mate!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9884412823336247621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3544589859" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3544589859" />
    <a title="Mak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66553282-mak"><img alt="Mak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546523711p2/66553282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3544589859?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mak" href="/user/show/66553282-mak">Mak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66553282-mak?shelf=smss">smss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3544589859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17178680385703278433">Another great read and once more a maelstrom of emotions. <br/><br/>Jeremy’s writing is his very signature. I believe I could recognize it anywhere: the proper English, the rich and beautiful vocabulary, the point of view by multiple characters, the back and forths, playing with the sense of time, the twists and cliffhangers, the absence of happy endings at least for those the readers usually root for, most villains get to outsmart the ‘good’ guys, even the lack of using ‘and’ to connect sentences, using </span>
  <span id="freeText17178680385703278433" style="display:none">Another great read and once more a maelstrom of emotions. <br /><br />Jeremy’s writing is his very signature. I believe I could recognize it anywhere: the proper English, the rich and beautiful vocabulary, the point of view by multiple characters, the back and forths, playing with the sense of time, the twists and cliffhangers, the absence of happy endings at least for those the readers usually root for, most villains get to outsmart the ‘good’ guys, even the lack of using ‘and’ to connect sentences, using a comma instead, and so much more. All of these together, some are just details and others more profound, along with the incredible way the world is built, the sceneries, the architecture, and of course the stories, make one extremely unique and amazing way of writing and an equally unique and amazing read! <br /><br />You begin reading the books always expecting something to amaze or shock you. I am sure, that everyone felt cocky while reading the Raven Heiress and were so sure they had spotted the deception at the very beginning. I don’t think there’s anyone who hadn’t realized who Arrandla was, as I don’t think anyone saw, not what would become of her, but, how the whole thing would end. The Higher of Evlon and the beautiful and eerie verse from the Book of Rivorder pointed to one direction and the Raven Heiress to another. <br /><br />The prologue starts with Lanixia Lowvilla Skysinger and her visit to Higher Durasian two days after his trial. It only makes sense for Durasian to be driven insane by his sorrow and the injustice towards him. Lanixia was unable to help him prove his innocence, but makes a plan on how to help him to a new life under a new identity on the Singing Isles. Right before it concludes, we get to see the first appearance of the infamous Salin Verse from the Book of Rivorder 5:8-10.<br /><br /><i>8When trouble rears itself against you, remember that in the beginning, when first I called you mine, I said, “I will hide you from your enemies.”9But now I will say this too; those who conspire against you, I will thwart, those who seek to destroy you will fail, 10for when my love is flared, there are none in this world who could do you harm.”<br />‘’What was it?’’.<br />‘’A Salin verse’’, said Jaydan, now seeming in deep thought. ‘’Rivorder 5:8-10’’. He regarded Lanixia. ‘’It looks as if your plans to rescue Durasian were not your plans after all. They were Adonai’s.’’ </i><br /><br />Then the story moves 982 years forward and more specifically to Evlon House where an interrogation is taking place. An incident has occurred and the story unfolds in a ‘Vantage point’ style where it is told by 3 different Elves. <br /><br />I knew there wasn’t going to be a happy ending, I always do, and still my heart breaks each time. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed the further introduction to this magnificent world. Each book offers further insight and by the time Upon the Sands is released it will be easier to comprehend whatever is to come. The writer not only describes the lands, monuments, cities, roads, rivers, people, but also mentions creatures such as mannaths, platheradons, menolves (plural of menolf?), taliants. He also mentions the different constellations and it is admirable, and even takes it a step further with a detailed description of the flags and banners of the various cities and islands. <br /><br /><i>The Avander’s Blade, an array of widely stretched out stars that took the shape of a sentinel’s longblade. The Star of Rivorder, one of the brightest and smallest in their solar system, the very one in which the Whispering God had used to guide the Reformer towards his refuge and salvation from Elder Paraden, the ancient Great Servant who’d persecuted the prophet. In addition, there was Fydran’s Wand, Drydan’s Eye, the Oliathor Stone, the Pilgar Flame. Lastly and most recently discovered, the Sandarian Star. </i><br /><br />I think words are not enough to do these books justice. I highly recommend them to anyone who enjoys High Fantasy, who can keep an open mind, who like puzzles and mind games and who can appreciate uniqueness and diversity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17178680385703278433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3546014971" class="review notext" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3546014971" />
    <a title="katayoun Masoodi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53974-katayoun-masoodi"><img alt="katayoun Masoodi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217161180p2/53974.jpg" /></a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WtmI0v1JsqSxHLg1ii5mg6r5BQoKjHeNNaf8FtNw4EqdPGr0hnIF574LVSab8x8PpiZvrAY4w4WyxAY8L4sLwA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F6LocGOixaBIQ4C3AiHMZswEQh7zA/oTxH2whqgrOBHQRwpWGJly40dUbaQT/LXqwNsouP+3ThtDHkqsVNDTmw==')})
  }

Here you have not a story of recovery but the day-by-day blast of fire it takes to choose life, or more accurately, to reclaim a body that’s been heisted, so much so that to feel anything a return to the body’s animal self is the only thing that works—sometimes by cutting but also by slipping into the skin of an alligator or growing antlers where her mother’s nails broke off in her scalp. Guess—holds the multiple facets of trauma up to the light with a piercing, rainbowed clarity. Linguistically taut, and imagistically deft, these lovely and harrowing poems linger and haunt. If you are a survivor, this is a book that will make you feel seen. If you are not a survivor, this is a book that will help you to see. Avery M. Guess is a stunning poet with a gorgeous talent, and a generously capacious heart. —Lee Ann Roripaugh, Author of Dandarians\n\nAvery Guess\'s debut collection of poems The Truth Is is a brave document of survivorhood. The poems bear witness to childhood domestic &amp; sexual violence, and ask the reader to listen with compassion, love, and tenderness. Formally varied, at turns, spare, narrative, and fantastical, the poems move with agility through possibility while refusing easy answers. Guess\'s book offers a necessary testimony for our times. —Cathy Linh Che, Author of Split\n\nIt is impossible to read the poems in this collection without taking a breath after each one, calculating everything at stake. The Truth Is dismantles our tidy narratives—its poems thrash with honesty, renouncing shame while demanding we, as readers, help carry the load.
